         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202410797-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f3b76480-2f6e-42b8-981b-6ad0bc7df8c7/adma202410797-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/f3b76480-2f6e-42b8-981b-6ad0bc7df8c7/adma202410797-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/8f9f8177-0958-47d4-99b7-2a019f9964e6/adma202410797-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f3b76480-2f6e-42b8-981b-6ad0bc7df8c7/adma202410797-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202410797-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202410797" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical properties of NMTP and NMTVP tested in half-cells. a) rate capability at 0.1–30 C, and the GCD curves of b) NMTVP and c) NMTP. d) cycling performance at 5 C. e) The average energy efficiencies of NMTVP and NMTP under different rates. f) The performance radar plot of NMTVP and NMTP. Investigations of Na-migration kinetics for NMTVP and NMTP. g) <i>D<sub>app,Na</sub></i> value of every redox peak calculated from CV tests and h) the GITT curves and calculated <i>D<sub>app,Na</sub></i> values.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>In-situ XRD was conducted to further investigate the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism in NMTVP by <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/7f5e8fb8-7c5f-41f6-86a9-c2a2651a672a/adma202410797-math-0022.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma202410797:adma202410797-math-0022" display="inline" location="graphic/adma202410797-math-0022.png">
               <semantics>
                  <msubsup>
                     <mi>Mn</mi>
                     <mi>Na</mi>
                     <mo>·</mo>
                  </msubsup>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${\mathrm{Mn}}_{{\mathrm{Na}}}^{\mathrm{\cdot}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math>-ASD regulation. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202410797-fig-0005">5a,c</a> shows the in situ XRD patterns of the NMTVP and NMTP cathodes in the range of 18–45° during the initial dis/charging process. We observed that the characteristic peaks at (104), (113), (024), (211), and (300) of both samples shifted during the dis/charging process, indicating the Na<sup>+</sup> de-intercalation process in the crystal and contraction and expansion of crystals. These continuous changes corresponded to the solid-solution reaction mechanism, demonstrating good structural reversibility. The peak at (104) gradually split into two peaks during the charging process, whereas those at (211) and (113) showed the opposite process; subsequently, these peaks reverted to their original state during the discharging process, indicating that both samples showed two-phase reactions. Notably, the peak at 2θ = 26° may be a back peak of beryllium (Be) that does not correspond to any crystal plane as the diffraction peaks remain unchanged the during electrochemical process and no similar diffraction peak is observed in the XRD analysis of powder samples. However, we clearly observed that the diffraction peak intensity of the phase transition reaction in NMTVP significantly decreased compared with that of NMTP, indicating that the electron-confinement-restrained strategy can inhibit phase transitions, thus stabilizing the crystal structure. Furthermore, the diffraction peaks at (113) and (211) of NMTP broadened when charged to ≈4.0&nbsp;V (yellow dashed line in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202410797-fig-0005">5c</a>), and a similar phenomenon was observed when NMTP was discharged to 2.6&nbsp;V. This phenomenon is attributed to lattice defects leading to the broadening of the Bragg reflection line, suggesting that NMTP cannot achieve a Please note that I have rectified the incorrect abbreviation in this case. Please note that I have rectified the incorrect abbreviation in this case.stable Na<sup>+</sup> de-intercalation process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202410797-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202410797-bib-0017_R_d145083698e1393" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Nano Energy">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In contrast, NMTVP shows minimal variation in the peak width as the interactions increase the Mn<sup>2+</sup> migration barrier and formation energy of the lattice defects. The variations in the lattice parameters (<i>a</i>, <i>c</i>, and <i>V</i>) with the state of charge were analyzed in NMTP and NMTVP to reveal the changes in crystal structure during the electrochemical process, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202410797-fig-0005">5b,d</a>. The lattice parameter <i>a</i> of both samples gradually decreased during charging and subsequently increased during the discharging process, corresponding to the initial shrinkage and subsequent expansion of the crystal structure along the <i>a</i>-axis. NMTP exhibited more significant shrinkage than NMTVP along the <i>c</i>-axis during the charging process. The <i>c</i>-axis of NMTVP exhibits an increasing trend. This may be ascribed to strong electron interactions between V and Mn along the <i>c</i>-axis. The NMTP cathode underwent significant structural changes owing to the two-phase reaction. Simultaneously, we observed volume changes (<i>ΔV/V</i> <sub>initial</sub>) from the original to the fully charged state of NMTP (9.68%) and NMTVP (9.46%). The smaller lattice variation proves that the electron-confinement-restrained strategy reduced the complex phase transition in NMTVP, inhibiting drastic changes in the crystal structure during the charging and discharging processes, thereby favoring a longer cycle.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202410797-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e9aed867-d700-49bd-bcf0-341078fca06a/adma202410797-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/e9aed867-d700-49bd-bcf0-341078fca06a/adma202410797-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/0f759cd7-7c3b-4797-9c7b-dc3d29dd708e/adma202410797-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e9aed867-d700-49bd-bcf0-341078fca06a/adma202410797-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202410797-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202410797" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a,c) In situ XRD patterns of structural evolution in two electrodes during cycling in the voltage window of 1.5–4.5&nbsp;V. b,d) Corresponding unit cell volume variation. e) Ex situ high-resolution XPS spectra at different charge/discharge states in NMTVP. f) XRD Rietveld refinement results of NMTVP and NMTP electrodes when discharged to 2.6&nbsp;V.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Additionally, ex-situ XPS was conducted to reveal the charge compensation mechanism of NMTVP. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202410797-fig-0005">5e</a>, the peak fitting results of the fine spectrum confirm the valence states of the different states.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202410797-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202410797-bib-0017_R_d145083698e1451" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Nano Energy">17</a>, <a href="#adma202410797-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202410797-bib-0023_R_d145083698e1451" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> From the open-circuit voltage (OCV) state to the fully charged state (4.3&nbsp;V), oxidation reactions of V<sup>3+/4+</sup>, Mn<sup>2+/3+</sup>, Mn<sup>3+/4+</sup>, and V<sup>4+/5+</sup> gradually occur. Ti is fully oxidized to Ti<sup>4+</sup> in the OCV state as the OCV is higher than that of Ti<sup>3+/4+</sup> (≈2.1&nbsp;V), and the + 4 oxidation state is maintained during the subsequent charging process. Correspondingly, successive reduction reactions of V<sup>5+/4+</sup>, Mn<sup>4+/3+</sup>, Mn<sup>3+/2+</sup>, V<sup>4+/3+</sup>, Ti<sup>4+/3+</sup>, and V<sup>3+/2+</sup> occurred during the discharge process. The orbital levels of V 2p, Mn 2p, and Ti 2p remain in the lowest oxidation states after discharging and contribute to the reversible capacity during subsequent cycles, and the multivalent state of V ensures sufficient Na<sup>+</sup> storage at high voltages. Rietveld refinement analysis for XRD was conducted to reveal the effect of <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/fd896c7d-5f74-4582-88ce-b15850e6d36e/adma202410797-math-0023.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma202410797:adma202410797-math-0023" display="inline" location="graphic/adma202410797-math-0023.png">
               <semantics>
                  <msubsup>
                     <mi>Mn</mi>
                     <mi>Na</mi>
                     <mo>·</mo>
                  </msubsup>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${\mathrm{Mn}}_{{\mathrm{Na}}}^{\mathrm{\cdot}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math>-ASD regulation. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202410797-fig-0005">5f</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a> (Supporting Information), show the comparison of Rietveld refinement of the XRD patterns of NMTP and NMTVP electrodes when discharged to 2.6&nbsp;V, suggesting a typical trigonal (<i>R-</i>3<i>c</i>) space group of cathodes, whereas aluminum (Al) adopts an <i>Fm-</i>3<i>m</i> space group with the smaller overall departure of <i>R<sub>wp</sub></i> and <i>χ<sup>2</sup></i>. A lower <i>R<sub>wp</sub></i> value indicated a better fit. This is because the electrode was still mainly based on the diffraction peaks of the NMTP and NMTVP materials, and the refined XRD model was included for the NASICON material and Al during the calculation. The atomic occupancies presented in Tables <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information) indicate the existence of Mn occupation for Na sites in NMTP that is mostly directed to the Na2 sites, proving that the formation of <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/0fad35cd-6f84-488a-820f-1ab4fd4f9c7c/adma202410797-math-0024.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma202410797:adma202410797-math-0024" display="inline" location="graphic/adma202410797-math-0024.png">
               <semantics>
                  <msubsup>
                     <mi>Mn</mi>
                     <mi>Na</mi>
                     <mo>·</mo>
                  </msubsup>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${\mathrm{Mn}}_{{\mathrm{Na}}}^{\mathrm{\cdot}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math>-ASD leads to undesirable voltage hysteresis. Correspondingly, the absence of Mn occupancy in NMTVP indicates that the electron-confinement-restrained strategy markedly inhibits the migration of Mn to eliminate voltage hysteresis.</p>
         
         <p>To ensure the excellent electrochemical performance of NMTVP in a half-cell, its practical feasibility was further evaluated on full-cell devices. Sodium-ion full cells (SIFCs) are assembled using an NMTVP cathode and a hard carbon (HC) anode, labeled HC//NMTVP (with HC//NMTP as the reference), as shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202410797-fig-0006">6a</a>. As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a> (Supporting Information), the Na storage performance of HC is tested in a half-cell in the voltage range of 0.01–3&nbsp;V, providing a reversible capacity of ≈278 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1 C. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202410797-fig-0006">6b</a> shows the typical GCD curves in the voltage window of 1.4–4.3&nbsp;V; HC//NMTVP delivers a reversible capacity of 159.73 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with an initial coulombic efficiency of ≈112.55%, which implies that the assembled SIFCs are well-matched. In contrast, HC//NMTP suffers from voltage hysteresis and delivers a reversible capacity of 129.67 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, which limits its practical application. Additionally, HC//NMTVP also exhibits excellent rate performance, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202410797-fig-0006">6c</a>, delivering reversible capacities of 136.92, 127.7, 121.3, 114.9, 104.7, 90, 74.74, and 60.92 mAh g<sup>− 1</sup> at 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, 10, and 20 C, respectively. Compared with those of the half-cells, the discharge capacity and rate performance of HC//NMTVP decreased. This was mainly attributed to the formation of a stable solid-electrolyte&nbsp;interphase (SEI) film and restraint of the HC anode at a high rate.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202410797-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202410797-bib-0024_R_d145083698e1563" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The specific capacity and energy density of HC//NMTVP at 0.1 C with a mean voltage of ≈2.92&nbsp;V and an energy density of 273.458&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> (based on the active mass of the cathode and anode) are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202410797-fig-0006">6d</a> and presented in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>. HC//NMTVP SIFCs are superior when assisted by electron-confinement compared with the advanced SIFCs reported thus far.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202410797-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202410797-bib-0006_R_d145083698e1577" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Nat. Commun. Nano Energy">6</a>, <a href="#adma202410797-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202410797-bib-0021_R_d145083698e1577" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - ACS Energy Lett. Small">21</a>, <a href="#adma202410797-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202410797-bib-0025_R_d145083698e1577" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Small Energy Storage Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. Adv. Mater. Nano Energy">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The capacity retention of 70.7% after 700 cycles at 2 C is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202410797-fig-0006">6e</a>, confirming the long-term cyclic stability of HC//NMTVP SIFCs. Therefore, the excellent full-cell performance of NMTVP makes it promising for large-scale practical applications in energy storage.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202410797-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/5d0c7728-9143-4a7f-ae72-1189f6c8d118/adma202410797-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/5d0c7728-9143-4a7f-ae72-1189f6c8d118/adma202410797-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/94711b5b-d0f4-4129-9321-24ec472e8f57/adma202410797-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/5d0c7728-9143-4a7f-ae72-1189f6c8d118/adma202410797-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202410797-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202410797" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance of SIFCs with NMTP and NMTVP cathodes. a) Schematic illustration of HC//NMTVP SIFCs. b) GCD curves at 0.1 C in the voltage range of 1.4–4.3&nbsp;V. c) Rate capability. d) The comparison of HC//NMTVP SIFCs with other reported full cells in terms of the voltage, capacity, and energy density. e) Long-term cycle performance at 2 C.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202410797-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202410797-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, we adopted the electronic confinement-restrained strategy to enable the regulation of <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/b644ad26-556a-4a61-8013-0bc161f99336/adma202410797-math-0025.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma202410797:adma202410797-math-0025" display="inline" location="graphic/adma202410797-math-0025.png">
               <semantics>
                  <msubsup>
                     <mi>Mn</mi>
                     <mi>Na</mi>
                     <mo>·</mo>
                  </msubsup>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${\mathrm{Mn}}_{{\mathrm{Na}}}^{\mathrm{\cdot}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math>-ASD, further eliminating the voltage hysteresis phenomenon in NMTP during the dis/charge process. XRD Rietveld refinement and SEM-EDS mappings demonstrated that V successfully entered the lattice, and the favorable confinement effect with electron-rich V substitution inhibited the migration of Mn. DFT confirmed that the vacancy formation energy and migration energy barriers of Mn increased owing to the electron interactions between V and Mn. Furthermore, we conducted a detailed analysis of the effects of electron confinement on electrochemical behavior. The prepared NMTVP cathode exhibited superior structural stability and rate performance, maintained a capacity retention of 92.3% after 1000 cycles at 10 C, and delivered a reversible capacity of 93.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 30 C. Simultaneously, NMTVP showed peak EE (89.5%) owing to the improvement of Mn redox activity. CV measurements at various scan rates, GITT technology, and in-situ XRD were employed to investigate the electrode kinetics and structural evolution. We found that the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics were enhanced and the phase transition reactions were reduced, stemming from the successful enablement of the regulation of <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/88a46729-daca-427d-bf58-50dad3617390/adma202410797-math-0026.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma202410797:adma202410797-math-0026" display="inline" location="graphic/adma202410797-math-0026.png">
               <semantics>
                  <msubsup>
                     <mi>Mn</mi>
                     <mi>Na</mi>
                     <mo>·</mo>
                  </msubsup>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${\mathrm{Mn}}_{{\mathrm{Na}}}^{\mathrm{\cdot}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math> ASD. The occupation of Na sites by Mn was also effectively suppressed by atomic occupancy in the crystal structure of the electrode when discharged to 2.6&nbsp;V. HC//NMTVP full cells exhibited impressive capacity and energy density, favoring their practical application. The electron-confinement-restrained strategy provides novel insights for addressing voltage hysteresis and developing high-energy NASICON cathode materials for SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
